9-24 BODY SERVICE

SEAT BELTS
SEAT BELTS SERVICING
Before doing the service or replacing seat belts, note the following
remarks:
• Belts must be in normal position with respect to the
retractor and/or buckle.
• Keep away belts from sharp objects or others damaging
them.
• Pay attention no to bend neither damage any buckle parts
and the belt tensioner.
• Avoid whitening or dye the belt. (Use only soft soap and
tepid water for cleaning).
• When installing the seat belt anchoring bolt, do it first by
hand to avoid damaging the thread.
• Don´t tray to repair the retracting mechanism or its cover.
Replace faulty pieces by new ones.
• Keep always belts dry and clean.
• If in doubt about the worthiness of any piece, replace it.
• Replace seat belts with sliced or damaged bands.
• Do not block the slit on panel through which the band passes.

Downloaded from www.Manualslib.com manuals search engine

BODY SERVICE 9-25

Removal
NOTE:
When replacing safety belt, change both the fixing buckle
and the belt retractor, with emergency blockage. This must
be done to be sure both the buckle and the small tongue
close properly.
If pieces were changed individually, if could happen that
they do not assemble properly.

1) Remove screws fixing safety belt ensemble to body.
2) Remove safety belt ensemble.

Instalation
1) Assemble safety belt unit reversing the dismantling order.

INSPECTION
Seat belts and fixing pieces might affect to important components
and systems of the vehicle.
Consequently, they must be carefully inspected and substituted
only by original pieces.
Inspect the followings components:
• Seat belt.
The strip or belt must be free.
• Retractor.
Should block the strip when pulling it fast. Beside, the
retractor should block strip when strip is inclined (approx
15°) in a longitudinal or transversal direction.
• Anchoring bolt.
Anchoring bolts must be tightened to the specified values.
• Belt hook.
Must stay blocked adequately.

BODY SERVICE 9-27

ANTICORROSION TREATMENT
Steel sheets have been previously treated for corrosion. To get a
higher resistance to corrosion inside and/or outside these are
galvanized both sides.
Because of greater protection against corrosion some
procedures are applied such as those described below:
1) Steel sheets have an electro cathodic priming to provide
greater resistance to corrosion.
2) A wax layer resistant to corrosion is applied to the internal
doors and the main lateral frames, where there is a tendency
to accumulate dampness.
3) A vinyl coating is applied in the lower part of the body and
inside of the wheel box.
4) A sealer is applied in the border of the door, connection of
plates in the engine compartment, and similar places, t o
avoid water entrance producing corrosion.
When steel plates are replaced, or when a repair is done after a
collision, if part of the repair is not treated, will be unprotected
against corrosion and getting damaged. Hence, it is essential
to do such protection when repairing the corresponding surfaces.
All the metal sheets are covered with metal conditioner and primer when they come out from the factory. When repairs are
done or pieces are replaced all the naked metal surfaces must
be cleaned and covered with rust proof primer. Do this work
before applying the sealer and the anticorrosion was coating.
Sealants are applied to specific unions of a vehicle during
manufacturing. The sealant blocks dust entrance in the vehicle
and acts as an anticorrosion barrier. Sealant is applied to the
door, the border of the bonnet and between panellings. If any
damages are repaired proper correction and fitting must be done.
Seal again the connection joints at a new replaced sheet and
the door border part or replaced bonnet.
Use quality sealants to seal the earflap unions, overlaying unions
and weldings. The sealant should be flexible and take on the
paint after putting it on the repaired areas.
To seal open unions, use an impermeable material. Select
sealant appropriate to such repair. Read the instruction given by
the manufacturer before using the sealant.
At times repair must be painted, in these cases follow the normal painting and finishing procedures.

Downloaded from www.Manualslib.com manuals search engine

9-28 BODY SERVICE

Anticorrosion wax is a penetrating compound applied to the metalmetal contact surfaces (door insides and main lateral frame)
where other coating material can not be used. Hence, when
choosing an anticorrosion wax it must be of the penetrating type.
When a vinyl protecting layer is applied, it must be done carefully
in order to avoid that the sealant comes in the motor, damper
ensemble and rotating pieces. After the protecting coating has
been applied, any draining holes within the body should be still
operational.
The sequence of work with anticorrosive materials is as follows:
1)
2)
3)
4)

Clean and prepare the metal surfaces.
Apply primer.
Apply sealer (all unions previously sealed).
Apply the adequate colour paint at all the part previously
coloured.
5) Apply anticorrosion compound (penetrating wax).
6) Apply protecting layer (rust proof material).
When welding or heating lead to burning of the original galvanic
protection or the anticorrosive materials in the surface, the
surfaces of internal sheets and under the bodywork must be
cleaned.
Cleaning of burning residues must be done carefully when the
place to be cleaned is box-like of any other form where access
to the inside is difficult. In general the following method can be
used.
WARNING:
Take all the usual cautions around a workshop,
specially protecting goggles, to avoid body risks
Scrape surfaces easily accessible. If a knife or a scraper does
not fit in place use a flexible scraper to access in difficult areas.
Compress air can eliminate many times most of the shavings
and is good when working in closed places. However, pay most
attention to wear protecting goggles.

Downloaded from www.Manualslib.com manuals search engine

BODY SERVICE 9-29

METALLIC SPARE PIECES FINISHING
Metallic spare pieces (or ensembles) are covered with
electrodeposited primer. To get good paint adhesion, the following
procedure is recommended).
1) Use wax or solvent degreaser to clean the piece.
2) Use damp or dry sandpaper (n° 400) to polish slightly the
sheet. Do not polish strongly to avoid scratches.
3) If the priming coating applied in the factory has been remove
exposing the metal, apply a metal conditioner for protection.
Read the manufacturer advices about how to use the metal
conditioner.
4) Apply the primer on dry surfaces before starting polishing
with sandpaper. Drying time is specified in the primer container.
5) Use damp or dry sandpaper (n° 400) to polish gently the
sheet.
6) Wash again this part.
7) Apply adequate colour paint on top.
8) Paints require different drying methods. Follow manufacturer
instructions indicated in the paint container.
9) When applying lacquer (fast drying paint layer), dry the
painted surface and polish with a polishing compound.
If melamine or acrylic is being used, no latter polishing after
drying is required.
10) If a lacquer coating is used, do no apply was on the covered
surface till full complete drying (about two months).
Before replacing pieces or external ensembles, check the paint
on all the covered surfaces or hidden interiors. If rust has set in
do as follows:
1) Use an adequate metal brush, blocker or antirust liquid to
eliminate corrosion. Follow the instruction given specially
for each of these materials.
2) If necessary, wash with detergent, rinse and dry.
3) Before assembling the body external pieces, apply an
anticorrosion compound in all the body external cleaned
surfaces. Anticorrosion compound must be applied too in
the internal surfaces of the body external sheets to be
assembled.

Downloaded from www.Manualslib.com manuals search engine

9-30 BODY SERVICE

FRAME
Each individual component of the framework has not only an
effect on the vehicle stiffness and but also in wheels alignment
(convergence, camber angle, castor angle).
Consequently, it is essential to carry out thorough surveys of
the framework, doing if necessary weldings related to its
correction or substitution.
When it is found that the plugging treatment or the anticorrosion
one on the framework are damaged, it is compulsory to repair
immediately followed by an anticorrosion treatment (see 9-27).
NOTE:
To check main dimensions of the frame, see the annexed
sketches.

Downloaded from www.Manualslib.com manuals search engine
